			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of cities by sunshine duration</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

</tr>
</table>
<p>The following is a <b>list of cities by sunshine duration</b>. <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_duration" title="Sunshine duration">Sunshine duration</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Climatological" class="mw-redirect" title="Climatological">climatological</a> indicator, measuring duration of <a href="/wiki/Sunshine" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunshine">sunshine</a> in given period (usually, a day or a year) for a given location on Earth, typically expressed as an averaged value over several years. It is a general indicator of <a href="/wiki/Cloud" title="Cloud">cloudiness</a> of a location, and thus differs from <a href="/wiki/Insolation" class="mw-redirect" title="Insolation">insolation</a>, which measures the total <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> delivered by sunlight over a given period.</p>
<p>Sunshine duration is usually expressed in hours per year, or in (average) hours per day. The first measure indicates the general sunniness of a location compared with other places, while the latter allows for comparison of sunshine in various seasons in the same location.<sup id="cite_ref-cimo_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cimo-1">[1]</a></sup> Another often-used measure is percentage ratio of recorded bright sunshine duration and <a href="#daylight_duration">daylight duration</a> in the observed period.</p>
<p>An important use of sunshine duration data is to characterize the climate of sites, especially of health resorts. This also takes into account the psychological effect of strong solar light on human well-being. It is often used to promote tourist destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-cimo_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cimo-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>
